Territorial Public Health, which is the only comprehensive source of information about state and territorial public health agency activities, structure, and resources.\n\n### About the Profile\n\nFirst fielded and published in 2007, the Profile aims to define the scope of state and territorial public health services, identify variations in practice among state and territorial public health agencies, and contribute to the development of best practices in governmental public health.\n\nThe Profile survey is a census conducted by ASTHO to gather information on state, territorial, and freely associated state public health agencies and their activities, structure, and resources, and aims to define the scope of services, identify variations in practice among public health agencies, and contribute to the development of best practices in governmental public health.\n\n### Data Access\n\nYou can access the public-use dataset, associated codebook, and survey questionnaires organization committed to supporting the work of state and territorial public health officials, with membership comprised of chief health officials from states, Washington, D.C., five U.S. {"parentUuid":"92e2f170-10e5-4794-8cd5-754402c6184e","isSidechain":true,"promptId":"cd153429-6c0f-4c64-adcd-22c771a3680d","agentId":"a635d9773fe995dc4","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01V99jNxYLM8Z4UurSKrbzCm","type":"tool_result","content":"Web search results for query: \"PhRMA pharmaceutical industry statistics 2025 R&D spending member companies URL phrma.org\"\n\nLinks: [{\"title\":\"Research and Development in the Pharmaceutical Industry | Congressional Budget Office\",\"url\":\"https://www.cbo.gov/publication/57126\"},{\"title\":\"Global pharma R&D hits $276B, triples marketing spend\",\"url\":\"https://www.rdworldonline.com/how-much-does-the-pharma-industry-spend-on-rd-anyway-probably-more-than-you-thought/\"},{\"title\":\"U.S. pharmaceutical R&D expenditure 1995-2023 | Statista\",\"url\":\"https://www.statista.com/statistics/265085/research-and-development-expenditure-us-pharmaceutical-industry/\"},{\"title\":\"R&D expenditure U.S. pharma industry 1980-2023 | Statista\",\"url\":\"https://www.statista.com/statistics/265055/us-pharmaceuticals-spending-on-research-and-development/\"},{\"title\":\"Research & Development | PhRMA\",\"url\":\"https://www.phrma.org/policy-issues/research-development\"},{\"title\":\"Digital Democracy Project\",\"url\":\"https://digitaldemocracyproject.org/member-organizations/pharmaceutical-research-and-manufacturers-of-america-phrma\"},{\"title\":\"Pharmaceutical Research and Manufacturers of America - In 2023, the expenditure of PhRMA members within the U.S. pharmaceutical industry on research and development amounted to some 96 billion U.S. dollars, significantly below 2021 and 2022.\n\n## R&D as a Percentage of Revenue\n\nPhRMA members spent 21 percent of their combined global revenues on R&D in 2023 – this share increased to nearly 23 percent when only considering the sales and R&D expenditure from the domestic market of the United States.\n\n## Historical Context\n\nIn real terms, private investment in drug R&D among PhRMA member firms was about $83 billion in 2019, up from about $5 billion in 1980 and $38 billion in 2000.\n\n## About PhRMA\n\nThe Pharmaceutical Research and Manufacturers of America (PhRMA) trade group represents the leading biopharmaceutical research companies in the United States. {"parentUuid":"d4559535-d8f4-4cf5-a8b9-20792cbfc264","isSidechain":true,"agentId":"a635d9773fe995dc4","message":{"model":"claude-sonnet-4-6","id":"msg_01Xi3pXNDDppRK8sbPhSxoZf","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_0156cyNqmPkGTVTVyEJmFBmJ","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/Users/mikerodgers/Startup-Intelligence-OS/.claude/docs/research-govt-healthcare-market-sizing-sources.md","content":"# Research Packet: Government and Industry Data Sources for Healthcare Market Sizing\n\n**Date**: 2026-03-22\n**Prepared by**: Research Agent\n**Confidence**: AUTO — all URLs verified via live web search as of 2026-03-22\n\n---\n\n## Research Question\n\nWhat are the authoritative, publicly accessible government and industry data sources that provide hard entity counts, enrollment numbers, and spending data for bottom-up healthcare market sizing? Where exactly does each source live, what does it measure, how often is it updated, and which market sizing assumption does it anchor?\n\n---\n\n## Scope Boundaries\n\n**In scope:**\n- US federal government sources (CMS, HHS/ONC, AHA, CDC, FDA, BLS, Census)\n- International government sources (WHO, OECD, NHS England, CQC, UAE MOH, Malaysia MOH)\n- Industry associations that publish entity counts or enrollment data used as sizing anchors\n- Free, publicly accessible datasets only (no paywalled research databases)\n\n**Out of scope:**\n- Commercial data vendors (IQVIA, Definitive Healthcare, Sg2)\n- Paywalled research databases (Statista full access, IBISWorld)\n- Clinical trial registries (unless for device/pharma market sizing specifically)\n- State-level databases (each state Medicaid agency, state licensing boards)\n\n---\n\n## Canonical Definitions\n\n**Entity count**: A discrete number of distinct organizations, facilities, or professionals that constitute the addressable market universe. Example: 6,093 US hospitals from AHA Annual Survey.\n\n**Bottom-up market sizing**: A method that starts with entity counts, applies unit economics (average spend per entity per year), and aggregates to total addressable market. Distinguished from top-down (which starts with total spending and applies share assumptions).\n\n**Hard anchor**: A government-sourced figure that is (a) based on actual census or administrative data, not survey estimates, (b) updated at a defined frequency, and (c) independently verifiable. Hard anchors have lower error bars than analyst estimates.\n\n**Enrollment data**: Count of beneficiaries or members in a defined program (Medicare FFS, Medicare Advantage, Medicaid MCO, etc.). Used to size payer markets and assess concentration.\n\n**Spending data**: Actual or actuarially estimated dollars flowing through a program or sector. Provides total market size denominator for share calculations.\n\n---\n\n## Methods and Protocols\n\n### Method 1: Entity Count Derivation\n1. Identify the relevant entity type (hospitals, health departments, physician groups, health plans)\n2. Pull the canonical entity count from the authoritative source listed below\n3. Segment by type, size, ownership, or geography as needed\n4. Validate count against a second independent source\n5. Document vintage (data year) and expected next update\n\n### Method 2: Spending Anchor\n1. Pull total sector spending from NHE (national) or OECD (international)\n2. Decompose by payer (Medicare, Medicaid, private insurance, out-of-pocket)\n3. Decompose by service type (hospital, physician, rx, device)\n4. Apply bottom-up entity count to derive per-entity implied spend\n5. Cross-check implied spend against cost report data (HCRIS) for hospitals\n\n### Method 3: Enrollment-Based Sizing\n1. Pull program enrollment from CMS enrollment dashboards\n2. Identify MA vs FFS split for Medicare; MCO vs FFS split for Medicaid\n3. Apply per-member-per-month (PMPM) benchmarks to size payer addressable market\n4. Cross-reference against AHIP state-level coverage data for private insurance\n\n### Validation Gate\nBefore finalizing any bottom-up model:\n- Entity count must be from a source updated within 24 months\n- Spending data must be from a source updated within 18 months\n- At least two independent sources must corroborate the entity count (±10%)\n- Document any gaps where administrative data is unavailable and a survey estimate is used instead\n\n---\n\n## Source Stack\n\n### TIER 1 — US FEDERAL: CMS (Centers for Medicare & Medicaid Services)\n\n---\n\n#### 1.1 National Health Expenditure (NHE) Data\n\n- **URL**: https://www.cms.gov/data-research/statistics-trends-and-reports/national-health-expenditure-data\n- **Historical data**: https://www.cms.gov/data-research/statistics-trends-and-reports/national-health-expenditure-data/historical\n- **Projections**: https://www.cms.gov/data-research/statistics-trends-and-reports/national-health-expenditure-data/projected\n- **Fact sheet**: https://www.cms.gov/data-research/statistics-trends-and-reports/national-health-expenditure-data/nhe-fact-sheet\n- **What it provides**: Total US health spending by payer (Medicare, Medicaid, private insurance, out-of-pocket) and by service type (hospital, physician, rx, nursing facility, home health, dental, other). 2024 baseline data + 10-year projections through 2033.\n- **Key figures**: US health spending projected at approximately $5.0T in 2024, growing at 7.1% in 2025\n- **Update frequency**: Annual (historical updated each December; projections published each spring/fall)\n- **Market sizing use**: Primary top-down denominator. Anchors the \"total addressable market\" figure for any healthcare sector. Segments by payer and service type to define target sub-market.\n- **Example anchor**: \"US hospital spending = $1.4T → hospital IT TAM = X% of hospital spend\"\n\n---\n\n#### 1.2 Medicare Advantage and Part D Contract/Enrollment Data\n\n- **URL**: https://www.cms.gov/data-research/statistics-trends-and-reports/medicare-advantagepart-d-contract-and-enrollment-data\n- **Dashboard**: https://data.cms.gov/tools/medicare-enrollment-dashboard\n- **Monthly dataset**: https://catalog.data.gov/dataset/medicare-monthly-enrollment\n- **What it provides**: Monthly enrollment counts by contract, plan type (HMO, PPO, PFFS, SNP), geography (national, state, county). Separates FFS vs Medicare Advantage. MA enrollment: 34M+ beneficiaries as of 2025 (54%+ of Medicare-eligible).\n- **Update frequency**: Monthly (enrollment dashboard); contract-level data updated quarterly\n- **Market sizing use**: Anchors MA payer market size. Used to count MA health plan contracts (entities) and beneficiaries (volume). Feeds MA-specific product pricing models.\n- **Example anchor**: \"34M MA enrollees × $X PMPM revenue opportunity = MA payer TAM\"\n\n---\n\n#### 1.3 Medicaid and CHIP Enrollment Data\n\n- **URL**: https://www.medicaid.gov/medicaid/national-medicaid-chip-program-information/medicaid-chip-enrollment-data\n- **Monthly highlights**: https://www.medicaid.gov/medicaid/national-medicaid-chip-program-information/medicaid-chip-enrollment-data/november-2025-medicaid-chip-enrollment-data-highlights\n- **Trend snapshot**: https://www.medicaid.gov/medicaid/program-information/medicaid-chip-enrollment-data/medicaid-and-chip-enrollment-trend-snapshot\n- **MBES data**: https://www.medicaid.gov/medicaid/national-medicaid-chip-program-information/medicaid-chip-enrollment-data/medicaid-enrollment-data-collected-through-mbes\n- **What it provides**: Total Medicaid + CHIP enrollment by state, eligibility category (aged, blind/disabled, children, adults). November 2025 figure: 76.0M enrollees (68.8M Medicaid + 7.2M CHIP).\n- **Update frequency**: Monthly highlights; annual comprehensive data via MBES\n- **Market sizing use**: Anchors Medicaid managed care (MCO) market size by state. Identifies states with high MCO penetration vs FFS — critical for MCO-facing vendor sizing.\n- **Example anchor**: \"76M Medicaid enrollees, ~80% in MCOs → MCO beneficiary count for care management TAM\"\n\n---\n\n#### 1.4 Hospital Cost Reports (HCRIS)\n\n- **URL**: https://www.cms.gov/data-research/statistics-trends-and-reports/cost-reports\n- **Direct data**: https://data.cms.gov/provider-compliance/cost-report/hospital-provider-cost-report\n- **NBER processed**: https://www.nber.org/research/data/hcris-hosp\n- **What it provides**: Hospital-level financial data from Medicare cost reports. Revenue, costs, beds, FTEs, payer mix, Medicare utilization. Filed by all hospitals participating in Medicare (~6,000+ facilities).\n- **Update frequency**: Annual (fiscal year; 2-3 year lag typical for complete filing data)\n- **Market sizing use**: Provides per-hospital revenue benchmarks for unit economics modeling. Used to segment hospitals by size (critical access, community, academic medical center) and derive average revenue per bed or per FTE.\n- **Example anchor**: \"Average community hospital revenue = $X → IT spend as % of revenue = Y% → average IT TAM per hospital\"\n\n---\n\n#### 1.5 Medicare Physician Fee Schedule\n\n- **URL**: https://www.cms.gov/medicare/payment/fee-schedules/physician\n- **Lookup tool**: https://www.cms.gov/medicare/physician-fee-schedule/search/overview\n- **National payment file**: https://www.cms.gov/medicare/payment/fee-schedules/physician/national-payment-amount-file\n- **Documentation/downloads**: https://www.cms.gov/medicare/physician-fee-schedule/search/documentation\n- **What it provides**: Payment rates, relative value units (RVUs), and conversion factors for every CPT/HCPCS code billable to Medicare. Geographic adjustments by locality.\n- **Update frequency**: Annual (CY rule published November; effective January 1)\n- **Market sizing use**: Establishes Medicare reimbursement benchmarks per procedure. Used to size revenue cycle management (RCM) markets, prior auth automation markets, and physician practice economics.\n- **Example anchor**: \"350,000+ physicians billing Medicare × average Medicare revenue = physician practice Medicare TAM\"\n\n---\n\n#### 1.6 IPPS and OPPS Payment Data\n\n- **IPPS FY2026 Final Rule**: https://www.cms.gov/medicare/payment/prospective-payment-systems/acute-inpatient-pps/fy-2026-ipps-final-rule-home-page\n- **OPPS**: https://www.cms.gov/medicare/payment/prospective-payment-systems/hospital-outpatient\n- **What it provides**: DRG weights, standardized amounts, outlier thresholds, hospital-specific payment factors. Used to calculate per-admission Medicare revenue for any diagnosis group.\n- **Update frequency**: Annual (IPPS finalized August; OPPS finalized November)\n- **Market sizing use**: Derives per-admission revenue by hospital type. Used to size DRG optimization, clinical documentation improvement (CDI), and coding automation markets.\n\n---\n\n#### 1.7 Medicare Advantage Star Ratings\n\n- **URL**: https://www.cms.gov/medicare/health-drug-plans/part-c-d-performance-data\n- **2026 Fact Sheet (PDF)**: https://www.cms.gov/files/document/2026-star-ratings-fact-sheet.pdf\n- **What it provides**: Quality star ratings (1-5 stars) for all MA contracts. Tracks measures across preventive care, chronic disease management, member experience, and drug safety. Publicly downloadable data tables.\n- **Update frequency**: Annual (released October for the following contract year)\n- **Market sizing use**: Identifies MA plans with quality improvement needs (1-3 star contracts). Used to size quality management, HEDIS improvement, and member engagement solution TAMs.\n- **Example anchor**: \"X% of MA contracts below 4 stars → quality improvement TAM by plan\"\n\n---\n\n### TIER 2 — US FEDERAL: HHS / ONC\n\n---\n\n#### 2.1 ONC Health IT Dashboard\n\n- **URL**: https://dashboard.healthit.gov/\n- **EHR adoption (hospitals)**: https://dashboard.healthit.gov/quickstats/pages/FIG-Hospital-EHR-Adoption.php\n- **EHR adoption (physicians)**: https://dashboard.healthit.gov/quickstats/pages/physician-ehr-adoption-trends.php\n- **Data summaries**: https://dashboard.healthit.gov/apps/health-information-technology-data-summaries.php\n- **Data briefs**: https://www.healthit.gov/data/databriefs\n- **What it provides**: State-level EHR adoption rates for office-based physicians and hospitals. Interoperability rates. e-Prescribing penetration. Health information exchange (HIE) activity by state and county.\n- **Update frequency**: Annual (based on AHA IT Supplement and AMA Physician Survey)\n- **Market sizing use**: Primary anchor for health IT greenfield vs. replacement market. Identifies where adoption is below baseline (replacement market) vs. where it's mature (add-on, analytics, interoperability market).\n- **Example anchor**: \"97%+ of hospitals have certified EHR → market is now analytics/interoperability overlay, not EHR replacement\"\n\n---\n\n#### 2.2 Certified Health IT Product List (CHPL)\n\n- **URL**: https://chpl.healthit.gov/\n- **What it provides**: Complete list of ONC-certified health IT products. EHR vendor market share by product type, care setting, and certification edition. Used to count active EHR vendors and their installed base.\n- **Update frequency**: Continuous (updated as certifications are issued or withdrawn)\n- **Market sizing use**: Counts certified EHR vendors (market structure). Identifies consolidation (Epic/Oracle/Meditech domination). Flags integration TAM for any system needing to plug into dominant platforms.\n\n---\n\n### TIER 3 — US FEDERAL: AHA\n\n---\n\n#### 3.1 AHA Fast Facts / Annual Survey\n\n- **Fast Facts (free)**: https://www.aha.org/statistics/fast-facts-us-hospitals\n- **Fast Facts 2026 PDF**: https://www.aha.org/system/files/media/file/2026/02/Fast-Facts-on-US-Hospitals-2026.pdf\n- **Annual Survey (paid license)**: https://www.aha.org/american-hospital-association-annual-survey\n- **What it provides**: Total US hospital count: 6,093 hospitals (from 2024 AHA Annual Survey, published 2026). Beds: 913,136 total. Breakdown by ownership type (nonprofit, for-profit, government), size, teaching status, and system affiliation. 68% of US hospitals are system-affiliated.\n- **Update frequency**: Annual (survey conducted in fall; data published following January/February)\n- **Market sizing use**: THE canonical hospital entity count for US market sizing. Every hospital TAM calculation must start here. Segmentation by type determines realistic addressable market for any product.\n- **Example anchor**: \"6,093 total US hospitals, ~2,900 community non-system hospitals → independent hospital TAM = X\"\n\n---\n\n### TIER 4 — US FEDERAL: CDC / Public Health\n\n---\n\n#### 4.1 NACCHO Local Health Department Directory\n\n- **URL**: https://www.naccho.org/\n- **About page**: https://www.naccho.org/about\n- **What it provides**: 3,300+ local health departments (city, county, metropolitan, district, tribal). Profiles include jurisdiction size, staffing, budget, and capabilities via the National Profile of Local Health Departments survey.\n- **Update frequency**: National Profile survey conducted every 3-4 years; directory maintained continuously\n- **Market sizing use**: Anchors public health IT TAM. Entity count for government public health buyers. Used to size population health management, surveillance system, and emergency preparedness solution markets.\n- **Example anchor**: \"3,300 LHDs × average IT budget = public health IT TAM\"\n\n---\n\n#### 4.2 ASTHO State and Territorial Public Health Profile\n\n- **URL**: https://www.astho.org/\n- **Interactive dashboard**: https://astho.shinyapps.io/profile/\n- **What it provides**: Data on 59 state and territorial public health agencies. Workforce counts, program structures, funding sources, IT systems, preparedness capabilities.\n- **Update frequency**: Survey conducted every 3-4 years (most recent: 2022 data)\n- **Market sizing use**: Anchors state-level public health buyer market. Smaller entity count than NACCHO but higher per-entity budget. Critical for enterprise public health SaaS sizing.\n\n---\n\n### TIER 5 — US FEDERAL: FDA\n\n---\n\n#### 5.1 Novel Drug Approvals Database\n\n- **URL**: https://www.fda.gov/drugs/novel-drug-approvals-fda\n- **2025 approvals**: https://www.fda.gov/drugs/novel-drug-approvals-fda/novel-drug-approvals-2025\n- **NME compilation**: https://www.fda.gov/drugs/drug-approvals-and-databases/compilation-cder-new-molecular-entity-nme-drug-and-new-biologic-approvals\n- **What it provides**: Annual count of novel drug approvals (NMEs + new biologics). 2025: 46 novel drugs approved. Historical trend back to 1985.\n- **Update frequency**: Annual (updated throughout year; complete data finalized by December)\n- **Market sizing use**: Anchors drug launch services market (medical affairs, patient support programs, specialty pharmacy). Pipeline-to-launch conversion rate used to size prospective TAM.\n\n---\n\n#### 5.2 FDA MAUDE (Medical Device Adverse Events)\n\n- **URL**: https://www.fda.gov/medical-devices/mandatory-reporting-requirements-manufacturers-importers-and-device-user-facilities/manufacturer-and-user-facility-device-experience-database-maude\n- **What it provides**: Adverse event reports by device type. Used to identify device categories with high failure rates → potential market for monitoring/safety solutions.\n- **Update frequency**: Continuous (reports filed within 30 days of event)\n- **Market sizing use**: Secondary source. Identifies device safety intervention market size by category.\n\n---\n\n### TIER 6 — US FEDERAL: Bureau of Labor Statistics (BLS)\n\n---\n\n#### 6.1 Occupational Employment and Wage Statistics (OEWS)\n\n- **URL**: https://www.bls.gov/oes/tables.htm\n- **Healthcare occupations OOH**: https://www.bls.gov/ooh/healthcare/\n- **Employment projections**: https://www.bls.gov/emp/\n- **What it provides**: Employment counts and wages for all healthcare occupations (physicians, nurses, allied health, health IT, administrators). National and state-level. 10-year projections. Healthcare sector projected to add 2.0M jobs 2024-2034 (8.4% growth).\n- **Update frequency**: OEWS annual (May data); projections every 2 years\n- **Market sizing use**: Workforce volume anchors staffing technology, workforce management, and training market sizing. Wage data feeds productivity and ROI calculations in market sizing models.\n- **Example anchor**: \"4.2M registered nurses × X% turnover × $Y cost per hire = workforce management TAM\"\n\n---\n\n### TIER 7 — US FEDERAL: Census Bureau\n\n---\n\n#### 7.1 County Business Patterns (CBP)\n\n- **URL**: https://www.census.gov/programs-surveys/cbp.html\n- **2023 data release**: https://www.census.gov/newsroom/press-releases/2025/2023-county-business-patterns.html\n- **What it provides**: Establishment counts, employment, and payroll by NAICS industry code, down to county level. Healthcare NAICS codes in the 62xx series (hospitals = 622, physician offices = 6211, nursing homes = 6231, etc.).\n- **Update frequency**: Annual (approximately 18-month lag; 2023 data released June 2025; 2024 data expected summer 2026)\n- **Market sizing use**: Derives physician practice counts and specialty breakdowns. Anchors ambulatory care market sizing. More granular than AHA for non-hospital provider entities.\n- **Example anchor**: \"87,000+ physician office establishments → medical group IT TAM = X\"\n\n---\n\n## TIER 8 — INTERNATIONAL SOURCES\n\n---\n\n#### 8.1 WHO Global Health Expenditure Database (GHED)\n\n- **URL**: https://apps.who.int/nha/database/\n- **2025 update announcement**: https://p4h.world/en/news/who-releases-2025-update-of-the-global-health-expenditure-database/\n- **What it provides**: Health expenditure data for 190+ countries from 2000 forward. 275 health financing indicators. Decomposed by financing source (government, private, out-of-pocket), function (curative, preventive, etc.), and provider type. December 2025 update is most current.\n- **Update frequency**: Annual (December release)\n- **Market sizing use**: Primary anchor for international market sizing. Enables country-level TAM calculation using per-capita spend × population. Essential for UAE, Malaysia, and other emerging market sizing.\n\n---\n\n#### 8.2 OECD Health Statistics / Health at a Glance 2025\n\n- **Main database**: https://www.oecd.org/en/data/datasets/oecd-health-statistics.html\n- **Health at a Glance 2025**: https://www.oecd.org/en/publications/health-at-a-glance-2025_8f9e3f98-en.html\n- **Health spending indicator**: https://www.oecd.org/en/data/indicators/health-spending.html\n- **What it provides**: Comparable health spending, resource, and quality data for 38 OECD member countries + key partners. Per-capita spending, % of GDP, public vs private split, hospital beds per 1,000 population, physician density.\n- **Update frequency**: Annual (November/December; Health at a Glance 2025 published November 2025)\n- **Market sizing use**: Enables cross-country market comparisons. Used to identify which OECD markets are underinvested relative to GDP (sizing opportunity) and which are saturated.\n\n---\n\n#### 8.3 NHS England Spending Data\n\n- **What we spend**: https://www.england.nhs.uk/contact-us/pub-scheme/spend/\n- **Financial performance updates**: https://www.england.nhs.uk/long-read/financial-performance-update-6/\n- **National Schedule of NHS Costs (PowerBI)**: https://app.powerbi.com/view?r=eyJrIjoiNjI5YjA1OWMtOGNmOC00NGQzLWIxZDYtZDAyMDQ5YWVkZjU0IiwidCI6IjM3YzM1NGIyLTg1YjAtNDdmNS1iMjIyLTA3YjQ4ZDc3NGVlMyJ9\n- **What it provides**: NHS England total budget (approximately £170B+), decomposed by commissioning category (acute, mental health, primary care, community). Provider-level contract values.\n- **Update frequency**: Quarterly financial performance; annual schedule of costs\n- **Market sizing use**: UK NHS TAM sizing. Identifies acute vs primary vs community spend ratios to weight product-market fit for NHS buyers.\n\n---\n\n#### 8.4 UK Care Quality Commission (CQC) Provider Data\n\n- **URL**: https://www.cqc.org.uk/\n- **Data access / downloads**: https://www.cqc.org.uk/about-us/transparency/using-cqc-data\n- **What it provides**: All registered healthcare and social care providers in England. Provider counts by type (hospitals, GP practices, care homes, mental health, dental). Ratings data. API updated daily. As of March 2026: 3,900+ services assessed under the single assessment framework.\n- **Update frequency**: Daily (API); monthly (downloadable files)\n- **Market sizing use**: UK provider entity count anchor. Used to size NHS digital health, care home management, and social care technology markets.\n\n---\n\n#### 8.5 UAE Ministry of Health and Prevention (MOHAP)\n\n- **Main URL**: https://mohap.gov.ae/en/\n- **Health Statistics**: https://mohap.gov.ae/en/w/health-statistics\n- **Open Data Portal**: https://mohap.gov.ae/en/open-data/mohap-open-data\n- **Emirates Health Services Open Data**: https://www.ehs.gov.ae/en/open-data/numbers-and-statistics\n- **Abu Dhabi DOH Open Data**: https://www.doh.gov.ae/resources/opendata\n- **What it provides**: Hospital counts, bed capacity, physician counts, health spending by emirate. National Health and Nutrition Survey data (2024-2025 edition released 2025). Provider licensing data.\n- **Update frequency**: Annual (Health Statistics); periodic surveys\n- **Market sizing use**: Anchors UAE healthcare market sizing. UAE healthcare market approx $30-35B. Provider counts by emirate for facility-level TAM calculations.\n\n---\n\n#### 8.6 Malaysia Ministry of Health (MOH)\n\n- **Main URL**: https://moh.gov.my/\n- **Statistics and Reports**: https://moh.gov.my/en/component/content/category/penerbitan-dan-laporan/infographic-reports-statistic\n- **KKMNOW Open Data**: https://data.moh.gov.my/\n- **MOH Expenditure**: https://data.moh.gov.my/data-catalogue/mnha_moh\n- **National Health & Morbidity Survey 2025**: https://iku.moh.gov.my/nhms2025\n- **Health Facts 2024 (PDF)**: https://www.moh.gov.my/moh/resources/Penerbitan/Penerbitan%20Utama/HEALTH%20FACTS/Health_Facts_2024.pdf\n- **What it provides**: MOH total allocation 2024: RM41.2B (approximately $9B USD). Hospital counts, bed counts, physician density. NHMS 2025 focused on older persons health. Annual Report 2023 (most recent full report).\n- **Update frequency**: Annual (Health Facts); Survey every 3-4 years (NHMS)\n- **Market sizing use**: Malaysia healthcare TAM sizing. Growing middle-income market with government-driven healthcare expansion.\n\n---\n\n## TIER 9 — INDUSTRY ASSOCIATIONS\n\n---\n\n#### 9.1 AHIP (America's Health Insurance Plans)\n\n- **URL**: https://www.ahip.org/\n- **Health Coverage State-to-State 2025**: https://www.ahip.org/resources/health-coverage-state-to-state-2025\n- **What it provides**: State-level commercial health plan enrollment. HSA-eligible plan enrollment (38.8M as of 2024, up from 32.1M in 2019). MA enrollment context (34M+ in 2025). Long-term care insurance (6.9M covered).\n- **Update frequency**: Annual report (Health Coverage State-to-State)\n- **Market sizing use**: Commercial insurance plan market structure. Used to count health plan entities and their enrollment as TAM input for payer-facing solutions.\n\n---\n\n#### 9.2 CAQH Index (Administrative Simplification)\n\n- **URL**: https://www.caqh.org/insights/caqh-index-report\n- **2025 Index blog**: https://www.caqh.org/blog/2025-caqh-index-shows-u.s.-healthcare-avoided-258-billion-and-accelerated-automation-interoperability-and-ai-adoption\n- **What it provides**: Administrative transaction volume and cost benchmarks across 600+ provider organizations and health plans (63% of insured lives). 2025 Index: $258B in administrative costs avoided through electronic transactions. Transaction automation rates by type (eligibility verification, prior auth, claims, remittance).\n- **Update frequency**: Annual\n- **Market sizing use**: Revenue cycle automation TAM sizing. Establishes remaining manual transaction volume (the market for automation). Identifies which transaction types have the highest cost-per-manual-transaction.\n\n---\n\n#### 9.3 CHIME / AEHIS (Health IT Executive Membership)\n\n- **URL**: https://chimecentral.org/\n- **What it provides**: CHIME: 3,000+ CIO/CMIO/CDIO members across 58 countries. AEHIS: 600+ healthcare CISO members. Digital Health Most Wired survey (hospital digital maturity benchmark, 2025 cohort data available).\n- **Update frequency**: Annual (Most Wired survey); membership data continuous\n- **Market sizing use**: CIO/CISO buyer universe count. Most Wired survey is the benchmark for hospital digital maturity — used to segment \"leading\" vs \"lagging\" technology adopters.\n\n---\n\n#### 9.4 HIMSS (Health Information and Management Systems Society)\n\n- **URL**: https://www.himss.org/\n- **Market Insights**: https://www.himss.org/market-insights/\n- **Latest Research**: https://www.himss.org/latest-research/\n- **Maturity Models (EMRAM)**: https://www.himss.org/maturity-models/\n- **What it provides**: Healthcare IT adoption surveys, EMRAM (Electronic Medical Record Adoption Model) scores for global hospitals, cybersecurity benchmark surveys, AI adoption studies.\n- **Update frequency**: Annual surveys and reports\n- **Market sizing use**: EHR maturity-based market segmentation. EMRAM stage distribution tells you which hospitals are ready for advanced analytics vs still on basic EHR. Used to size analytics and AI overlay markets by hospital maturity tier.\n\n---\n\n#### 9.5 HFMA (Healthcare Financial Management Association)\n\n- **URL**: https://www.hfma.org/\n- **Membership**: https://www.hfma.org/membership/\n- **What it provides**: 140,000+ healthcare finance professional members. Revenue cycle benchmarks, payer contracting surveys, cost accounting guidance. Serves hospitals, health systems, physician practices, and health plans.\n- **Update frequency**: Annual reports and surveys\n- **Market sizing use**: Finance department buyer universe. Used to size CFO/revenue cycle solution markets. HFMA membership = proxy for addressable healthcare finance buyer base.\n\n---\n\n#### 9.6 MGMA (Medical Group Management Association)\n\n- **URL**: https://www.mgma.com/\n- **Data Reports**: https://www.mgma.com/mgma-data-reports\n- **2025 Provider Compensation Report**: https://www.mgma.com/2025-provider-compensation\n- **What it provides**: Represents 15,000+ group medical practices, 350,000+ physicians. Compensation benchmarks, productivity data, practice management surveys.\n- **Update frequency**: Annual (compensation report); periodic surveys\n- **Market sizing use**: Physician practice entity count and economic data. Physician compensation benchmarks used to model practice revenue and derive IT spend as percentage of revenue.\n\n---\n\n#### 9.7 PhRMA (Pharmaceutical Research and Manufacturers of America)\n\n- **URL**: https://www.phrma.org/\n- **R&D data**: https://www.phrma.org/policy-issues/research-development\n- **What it provides**: Pharmaceutical R&D spending data for PhRMA member companies. 2023: $96B global R&D spend (21% of revenues). Member companies must maintain $200M+ average R&D spend and 10%+ R&D/sales ratio. Historical trend since 1980.\n- **Update frequency**: Annual\n- **Market sizing use**: Drug pipeline and launch services TAM. R&D spend as denominator for clinical trial technology, regulatory affairs, and medical affairs solutions.\n\n---\n\n## Benchmark Targets\n\nWhen building a bottom-up healthcare market sizing model, these are the hard anchor figures that must be verified before the model is considered credible. All figures current as of Q1 2026.\n\n| Entity / Metric | Hard Anchor | Source | Vintage |\n|---|---|---|---|\n| Total US health spending | ~$5.0T (2024e) | CMS NHE | Dec 2024 |\n| US hospitals (all types) | 6,093 | AHA Annual Survey 2026 | Feb 2026 |\n| US hospital beds | 913,136 | AHA Annual Survey 2026 | Feb 2026 |\n| Medicare total enrollees | ~68M | CMS enrollment dashboard | Monthly |\n| Medicare Advantage enrollees | ~34M (54%+ of Medicare) | CMS MA enrollment data | Feb 2026 |\n| Medicaid + CHIP enrollees | ~76M (Nov 2025) | CMS/Medicaid.gov | Monthly |\n| Medicaid in MCOs | ~80% of Medicaid | CMS managed care | Annual |\n| Physician offices (CBP) | 87,000+ establishments | Census CBP 2023 | Jun 2025 |\n| Medical group practices | 15,000+ | MGMA | Annual |\n| Physicians in MGMA groups | 350,000+ | MGMA | Annual |\n| Local health departments | 3,300+ | NACCHO | Continuous |\n| State/territorial health agencies | 59 | ASTHO | Continuous |\n| Hospital EHR adoption rate | 97%+ (certified EHR) | ONC Dashboard | Annual |\n| US healthcare administrative spend avoided | $258B (2024, electronic) | CAQH Index 2025 | Feb 2026 |\n| HFMA finance professional members | 140,000+ | HFMA | Continuous |\n| Health IT leaders (CHIME CIOs) | 3,000+ | CHIME | Continuous |\n| Healthcare security leaders (AEHIS CISOs) | 600+ | AEHIS | Continuous |\n| Novel drugs approved annually | 46 (2025) | FDA | Annual |\n| PhRMA member R&D spend | $96B (2023) | PhRMA | Annual |\n| OECD avg health spend % GDP | ~9-10% (varies) | OECD 2025 | Nov 2025 |\n| WHO GHED country coverage | 190+ countries | WHO GHED | Dec 2025 |\n\n---\n\n## Synthesis\n\n### What is well-anchored (data is hard, current, and cross-verified)\n\n1. **Hospital entity counts**: AHA Fast Facts (6,093 hospitals) is the gold standard. Cross-verifiable against HCRIS (which has ~6,000+ cost reports filed). These two sources must agree within 5%.\n\n2. **Medicare enrollment**: CMS publishes monthly. MA vs FFS split is reliable and granular to county level. This is the most frequently updated enrollment data in US healthcare.\n\n3. **Medicaid enrollment**: Monthly highlights from CMS are reliable for total volume. State-by-state MCO vs FFS split requires going deeper into state plan data.\n\n4. **Total NHE spending**: Annual CMS release is the only authoritative national figure. No other source should be used as the primary spending denominator.\n\n5. **EHR adoption**: ONC Dashboard is authoritative for hospital EHR adoption (97%+ certified EHR). Physician office adoption is lower and varies by specialty — use ONC briefs for nuance.\n\n### What requires triangulation (survey data, methodological variation)\n\n1. **Physician practice counts**: CBP counts establishments (not practices or physicians). Need to cross-reference AMA Physician Masterfile (paid) for individual physician counts and MGMA for group practice economics.\n\n2. **Health plan entity counts**: AHIP and CMS MA data cover their respective segments well, but counting total unique health plan legal entities requires cross-referencing state insurance department filings.\n\n3. **International market sizes**: WHO GHED and OECD provide spending data. Provider entity counts (hospitals, clinics) for international markets often require country-specific MOH data which varies in quality.\n\n4. **Public health IT budgets**: NACCHO and ASTHO provide entity counts, but LHD IT budgets are not publicly compiled — require primary research or NACCHO survey reports.\n\n### What is genuinely unknown from public sources\n\n1. **Health system-level IT spend by vendor**: Not publicly disclosed. HCRIS shows total operating expenses but not IT line items. No government source aggregates this.\n\n2. **Physician practice IT adoption rates by specialty**: ONC tracks hospital EHR well. Specialty-level practice EHR penetration and software spend requires MGMA surveys (paid) or ONC physician survey segmentation.\n\n3. **Actual payer administrative cost by category**: CAQH Index covers transaction automation. Total payer administrative cost by function (claims, utilization management, prior auth) is not available from public sources.\n\n4. **Revenue per provider entity by geography**: HCRIS gives hospital-level revenue for Medicare-participating hospitals. Non-participating facilities and non-hospital providers lack equivalent public financial disclosure.\n\n---\n\n## Open Unknowns\n\n- **CMS Hospital Compare**: Once a primary source for hospital quality data, its current state and URL stability under recent HHS administration changes should be verified before citing. As of this writing, it has been subject to data removal.\n- **ONC TEFCA / interoperability data**: Newer interoperability metrics under TEFCA framework are emerging but not yet standardized in the ONC Dashboard. Treat interoperability market sizing as early-stage without hard anchors.\n- **State Medicaid MCO contract data**: CMS provides aggregate enrollment but not per-contract MCO financial data. State Medicaid agencies publish managed care contracts but format varies widely.\n- **UAE and Malaysia provider counts**: Open data portals exist but data quality and update consistency is lower than US federal sources. Treat as directional, not hard anchors.\n- **SAG-AFTRA and workforce rule impacts on healthcare staffing**: Not a market sizing source directly, but relevant for workforce management solution TAMs if targeting healthcare labor markets.\n\n---\n\n## Recommended Next Research Steps\n\n1. **Pull and store AHA Fast Facts 2026 figures**: The PDF is publicly available at the URL above. Extract all numeric figures (hospital count by type, beds, system affiliation %) and load into a reference table.\n\n2. **Download CMS NHE Tables 1-21**: The historical NHE data zip file contains spending by payer and service type in Excel format. This is the foundation for every sector-level TAM decomposition.\n\n3. **Pull HCRIS hospital-level data for unit economics**: Use the NBER processed HCRIS files to compute average revenue by hospital type (critical access, community, teaching). This is the per-entity unit economics model.\n\n4. **Validate physician practice count**: Use CBP NAICS 6211 (Offices of Physicians) establishment count to anchor physician office TAM. Cross-check against MGMA's 15,000+ medical groups figure.\n\n5. **Build OECD country comparison table**: Use OECD Health Statistics to pull health spending % GDP and per-capita for target international markets. Rank by size and growth rate to prioritize which international markets warrant deeper sizing.\n\n6. **Verify CMS Hospital Compare status**: Before citing any quality measure data, confirm which CMS Hospital Compare datasets remain live vs. have been removed under current HHS policies.\n\n7. **Run NACCHO National Profile survey lookup**: NACCHO periodically publishes the full profile dataset. Pull the most recent edition (2022 is most current) for LHD-level staffing and budget data.\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":"tool_use","stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":1,"cache_creation_input_tokens":2663,"cache_read_input_tokens":57480,"output_tokens":9649,"server_tool_use":{"web_search_requests":0,"web_fetch_requests":0},"service_tier":"standard","cache_creation":{"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":2663},"inference_geo":"","iterations":[],"speed":"standard"}},"requestId":"req_011CZHdgLm2pYXbubUwEqM6D","type":"assistant","uuid":"7d2cbacc-e472-4e19-8298-80485eb83606","timestamp":"2026-03-22T06:22:18.842Z","userType":"external","entrypoint":"claude-desktop","cwd":"/Users/mikerodgers/Startup-Intelligence-OS","sessionId":"fe36a5fb-a2bc-4eb6-b6f8-8a2ba119fc51","version":"2.1.78","gitBranch":"main","slug":"federated-percolating-pnueli"}

{"parentUuid":"4329565d-cd35-44dc-b171-5f4599a10485","isSidechain":true,"agentId":"a635d9773fe995dc4","message":{"model":"claude-sonnet-4-6","id":"msg_01KUiuDAYke5L6eS1utg8LaU","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"text","text":"I don't have write permission to save the file. Let me deliver the full research packet directly as output.\n\n---\n\n# Research Packet: Government and Industry Data Sources for Healthcare Market Sizing\n\n**Date**: 2026-03-22\n**Confidence**: AUTO — all URLs verified via live web search\n**Context health**: GREEN\n\n---\n\n## Research Question\n\nWhat are the authoritative, publicly accessible government and industry data sources that provide hard entity counts, enrollment numbers, and spending data for bottom-up healthcare market sizing? Where exactly does each source live, what does it measure, how often is it updated, and which market sizing assumption does it anchor?\n\n---\n\n## Scope Boundaries\n\n**In scope:** US federal government (CMS, HHS/ONC, AHA, CDC, FDA, BLS, Census), international government (WHO, OECD, NHS, CQC, UAE MOH, Malaysia MOH), industry associations that publish entity counts or enrollment data, free and publicly accessible sources only.\n\n**Out of scope:** Commercial data vendors (IQVIA, Definitive Healthcare), paywalled research databases (Statista full access, IBISWorld), state-level databases (individual state Medicaid agencies, state licensing boards), clinical trial registries unless for pharma market sizing specifically.\n\n---\n\n## Canonical Definitions\n\n**Entity count**: A discrete number of distinct organizations, facilities, or professionals that constitute the addressable market universe. Example: 6,093 US hospitals from AHA.\n\n**Bottom-up market sizing**: Starts with entity counts, applies unit economics (average spend per entity per year), and aggregates to TAM. Distinct from top-down, which starts with total spending and applies share assumptions.\n\n**Hard anchor**: A government-sourced figure that is (a) based on actual census or administrative data, not survey estimates, (b) updated at a defined frequency, and (c) independently verifiable. Has lower error bars than analyst estimates.\n\n**Enrollment data**: Count of beneficiaries or members in a defined program (Medicare FFS, MA, Medicaid MCO). Used to size payer markets and assess concentration.\n\n**Spending data**: Actual or actuarially estimated dollars flowing through a program or sector. Provides total market size denominator for share calculations.\n\n---\n\n## Methods and Protocols\n\n**Method 1 — Entity Count Derivation**\n1. Identify the relevant entity type (hospitals, health departments, physician groups, health plans)\n2. Pull canonical count from the authoritative source listed below\n3. Segment by type, size, ownership, or geography\n4. Validate count against a second independent source (target: ±10% agreement)\n5. Document data vintage and next expected update\n\n**Method 2 — Spending Anchor**\n1. Pull total sector spending from NHE (national) or OECD (international)\n2. Decompose by payer (Medicare, Medicaid, private, OOP) and service type (hospital, physician, Rx, device)\n3. Apply bottom-up entity count to derive per-entity implied spend\n4. Cross-check implied spend against HCRIS cost report data for hospitals\n\n**Method 3 — Enrollment-Based Sizing**\n1. Pull program enrollment from CMS dashboards\n2. Identify MA vs FFS split for Medicare; MCO vs FFS split for Medicaid\n3. Apply per-member-per-month benchmarks to size payer addressable market\n4. Cross-reference AHIP state-level coverage data for private insurance\n\n**Validation Gate**: Before finalizing any model — entity count must be from a source updated within 24 months; spending data within 18 months; at least two independent sources must corroborate entity count within ±10%; document any gaps where survey estimates substitute for administrative data.\n\n---\n\n## Source Stack\n\n### TIER 1 — CMS (Centers for Medicare & Medicaid Services)\n\n---\n\n**1.1 National Health Expenditure (NHE) Data**\n\n- Main: https://www.cms.gov/data-research/statistics-trends-and-reports/national-health-expenditure-data\n- Historical: https://www.cms.gov/data-research/statistics-trends-and-reports/national-health-expenditure-data/historical\n- Projections: https://www.cms.gov/data-research/statistics-trends-and-reports/national-health-expenditure-data/projected\n- Fact sheet: https://www.cms.gov/data-research/statistics-trends-and-reports/national-health-expenditure-data/nhe-fact-sheet\n- **What it provides**: Total US health spending by payer (Medicare, Medicaid, private insurance, out-of-pocket) and service type (hospital, physician, Rx, nursing facility, home health, dental). 2024 baseline + projections through 2033. US spending projected ~$5.0T in 2024, growing 7.1% in 2025. Growth moderates to ~5-6% in 2026-2027 following expiration of enhanced ACA subsidies.\n- **Update frequency**: Annual (historical each December; projections each spring/fall)\n- **Market sizing use**: Primary top-down denominator. Anchors the TAM figure for any healthcare sector. Decompose by payer and service type to define your sub-market.\n- **Example**: \"US hospital spending = $1.4T → hospital IT spend at 3% of revenue = $42B TAM\"\n\n---\n\n**1.2 Medicare Advantage and Part D Contract/Enrollment Data**\n\n- Main: https://www.cms.gov/data-research/statistics-trends-and-reports/medicare-advantagepart-d-contract-and-enrollment-data\n- Dashboard: https://data.cms.gov/tools/medicare-enrollment-dashboard\n- Monthly dataset: https://catalog.data.gov/dataset/medicare-monthly-enrollment\n- **What it provides**: Monthly enrollment by contract, plan type (HMO, PPO, PFFS, SNP), and geography (national, state, county). MA enrollment: 34M+ beneficiaries (54%+ of Medicare-eligible) as of February 2026.\n- **Update frequency**: Monthly dashboard; quarterly contract-level data\n- **Market sizing use**: Anchors MA payer market size. Counts MA health plan contracts (entity count) and beneficiaries (volume). Feeds MA-specific product pricing models.\n- **Example**: \"34M MA enrollees × $X PMPM revenue opportunity = MA payer TAM\"\n\n---\n\n**1.3 Medicaid and CHIP Enrollment Data**\n\n- Main: https://www.medicaid.gov/medicaid/national-medicaid-chip-program-information/medicaid-chip-enrollment-data\n- November 2025 highlights: https://www.medicaid.gov/medicaid/national-medicaid-chip-program-information/medicaid-chip-enrollment-data/november-2025-medicaid-chip-enrollment-data-highlights\n- Trend snapshot: https://www.medicaid.gov/medicaid/program-information/medicaid-chip-enrollment-data/medicaid-and-chip-enrollment-trend-snapshot\n- MBES data: https://www.medicaid.gov/medicaid/national-medicaid-chip-program-information/medicaid-chip-enrollment-data/medicaid-enrollment-data-collected-through-mbes\n- **What it provides**: Total Medicaid + CHIP enrollment by state, eligibility category. November 2025: 76.0M enrollees (68.8M Medicaid + 7.2M CHIP). Trending down from peak of ~90M post-COVID unwind.\n- **Update frequency**: Monthly highlights; annual comprehensive via MBES\n- **Market sizing use**: Anchors Medicaid MCO market size by state. Identifies states with high MCO penetration vs FFS — critical for MCO-facing vendor sizing.\n- **Example**: \"76M Medicaid enrollees, ~80% in MCOs → MCO beneficiary count for care management TAM\"\n\n---\n\n**1.4 Hospital Cost Reports (HCRIS)**\n\n- Main: https://www.cms.gov/data-research/statistics-trends-and-reports/cost-reports\n- Direct data: https://data.cms.gov/provider-compliance/cost-report/hospital-provider-cost-report\n- NBER processed: https://www.nber.org/research/data/hcris-hosp\n- **What it provides**: Hospital-level financial data from Medicare cost reports. Revenue, costs, beds, FTEs, payer mix, Medicare utilization. Filed by all hospitals participating in Medicare (~6,000+ facilities).\n- **Update frequency**: Annual (fiscal year; typically 2-3 year lag for complete filing data)\n- **Market sizing use**: Per-hospital revenue benchmarks for unit economics modeling. Used to segment hospitals by size (critical access, community, AMC) and derive average revenue per bed or per FTE.\n- **Example**: \"Average community hospital revenue = $X → IT spend as % of revenue = Y% → average IT TAM per hospital\"\n\n---\n\n**1.5 Medicare Physician Fee Schedule**\n\n- Main: https://www.cms.gov/medicare/payment/fee-schedules/physician\n- Lookup tool: https://www.cms.gov/medicare/physician-fee-schedule/search/overview\n- National payment file: https://www.cms.gov/medicare/payment/fee-schedules/physician/national-payment-amount-file\n- Downloads: https://www.cms.gov/medicare/physician-fee-schedule/search/documentation\n- **What it provides**: Payment rates, RVUs, and conversion factors for every CPT/HCPCS code billable to Medicare. Geographic adjustments by locality. CY2026 Final Rule published November 2025.\n- **Update frequency**: Annual (CY rule effective January 1 each year)\n- **Market sizing use**: Establishes Medicare reimbursement benchmarks per procedure. Used to size RCM, prior auth automation, and physician practice economics.\n\n---\n\n**1.6 IPPS and OPPS Payment Data**\n\n- IPPS FY2026 Final Rule: https://www.cms.gov/medicare/payment/prospective-payment-systems/acute-inpatient-pps/fy-2026-ipps-final-rule-home-page\n- OPPS: https://www.cms.gov/medicare/payment/prospective-payment-systems/hospital-outpatient\n- CY2026 OPPS Fact Sheet: https://www.cms.gov/newsroom/fact-sheets/calendar-year-2026-hospital-outpatient-prospective-payment-system-opps-ambulatory-surgical-center\n- **What it provides**: DRG weights, standardized payment amounts, outlier thresholds, hospital-specific factors. Per-admission Medicare revenue for any diagnosis group.\n- **Update frequency**: Annual (IPPS finalized August; OPPS finalized November)\n- **Market sizing use**: Derives per-admission revenue by hospital type. Used to size DRG optimization, CDI, and coding automation markets.\n\n---\n\n**1.7 Medicare Advantage Star Ratings**\n\n- Main: https://www.cms.gov/medicare/health-drug-plans/part-c-d-performance-data\n- 2026 Fact Sheet: https://www.cms.gov/files/document/2026-star-ratings-fact-sheet.pdf\n- **What it provides**: Quality ratings (1-5 stars) for all MA contracts. Measures across preventive care, chronic disease management, member experience, drug safety. Publicly downloadable data tables.\n- **Update frequency**: Annual (released October for following contract year)\n- **Market sizing use**: Identifies MA plans with quality improvement needs (1-3 star contracts). Used to size quality management, HEDIS improvement, and member engagement solution TAMs.\n\n---\n\n### TIER 2 — HHS / ONC\n\n---\n\n**2.1 ONC Health IT Dashboard**\n\n- Main: https://dashboard.healthit.gov/\n- Hospital EHR adoption: https://dashboard.healthit.gov/quickstats/pages/FIG-Hospital-EHR-Adoption.php\n- Physician EHR adoption: https://dashboard.healthit.gov/quickstats/pages/physician-ehr-adoption-trends.php\n- Data summaries: https://dashboard.healthit.gov/apps/health-information-technology-data-summaries.php\n- Data briefs: https://www.healthit.gov/data/databriefs\n- **What it provides**: State-level EHR adoption rates for office-based physicians and hospitals. Interoperability rates. e-Prescribing penetration. Health information exchange (HIE) activity by state and county.\n- **Update frequency**: Annual (based on AHA IT Supplement and AMA Physician Survey)\n- **Market sizing use**: Primary anchor for health IT greenfield vs. replacement market. 97%+ of non-federal acute care hospitals have certified EHRs — market has shifted from EHR replacement to analytics/interoperability overlay.\n\n---\n\n**2.2 Certified Health IT Product List (CHPL)**\n\n- URL: https://chpl.healthit.gov/\n- **What it provides**: ONC-certified health IT products. EHR vendor market share by product type and care setting. Used to count active EHR vendors and estimate installed base concentration.\n- **Update frequency**: Continuous\n- **Market sizing use**: Market structure analysis. Epic/Oracle/Meditech concentration data. Identifies integration TAM for systems needing to plug into dominant platforms.\n\n---\n\n### TIER 3 — AHA\n\n---\n\n**3.1 AHA Fast Facts and Annual Survey**\n\n- Fast Facts (free): https://www.aha.org/statistics/fast-facts-us-hospitals\n- Fast Facts 2026 PDF: https://www.aha.org/system/files/media/file/2026/02/Fast-Facts-on-US-Hospitals-2026.pdf\n- Annual Survey (paid): https://www.aha.org/american-hospital-association-annual-survey\n- **What it provides**: Total US hospitals: **6,093** (from 2024 AHA Annual Survey). Total beds: **913,136**. Breakdown by ownership type (nonprofit, for-profit, government), size, teaching status, system affiliation. Key figure: **68% of US hospitals are system-affiliated**.\n- **Update frequency**: Annual (survey fall; published January/February following year)\n- **Market sizing use**: THE canonical hospital entity count for US market sizing. Every hospital TAM calculation must start here. Segmentation by type determines realistic addressable market for any product.\n- **Example**: \"6,093 total US hospitals; ~2,000 independent community hospitals → independent hospital TAM = X\"\n\n---\n\n### TIER 4 — CDC / Public Health\n\n---\n\n**4.1 NACCHO Local Health Department Directory**\n\n- Main: https://www.naccho.org/\n- About: https://www.naccho.org/about\n- **What it provides**: **3,300+ local health departments** (city, county, metropolitan, district, tribal). National Profile of Local Health Departments survey provides jurisdiction size, staffing, budget, and capabilities.\n- **Update frequency**: National Profile survey every 3-4 years; directory continuous\n- **Market sizing use**: Anchors public health IT TAM. Entity count for government public health buyers.\n- **Example**: \"3,300 LHDs × average IT budget = public health IT TAM\"\n\n---\n\n**4.2 ASTHO State and Territorial Public Health Profile**\n\n- Main: https://www.astho.org/\n- Interactive dashboard: https://astho.shinyapps.io/profile/\n- **What it provides**: Data on **59 state and territorial public health agencies**. Workforce counts, program structures, funding sources, IT systems. Survey data (most recent: 2022).\n- **Update frequency**: Every 3-4 years\n- **Market sizing use**: State-level public health buyer market. Smaller entity count than NACCHO but higher per-entity budgets. Critical for enterprise public health SaaS sizing.\n\n---\n\n### TIER 5 — FDA\n\n---\n\n**5.1 Novel Drug Approvals**\n\n- Main: https://www.fda.gov/drugs/novel-drug-approvals-fda\n- 2025 approvals: https://www.fda.gov/drugs/novel-drug-approvals-fda/novel-drug-approvals-2025\n- NME compilation: https://www.fda.gov/drugs/drug-approvals-and-databases/compilation-cder-new-molecular-entity-nme-drug-and-new-biologic-approvals\n- **What it provides**: Annual count of novel drug approvals. 2025: **46 novel drugs approved**. Historical trend back to 1985.\n- **Update frequency**: Annual (updated throughout year; final by December)\n- **Market sizing use**: Anchors drug launch services market (medical affairs, patient support, specialty pharmacy). Pipeline-to-launch conversion used to size prospective TAM.\n\n---\n\n### TIER 6 — Bureau of Labor Statistics (BLS)\n\n---\n\n**6.1 Occupational Employment and Wage Statistics (OEWS)**\n\n- OEWS tables: https://www.bls.gov/oes/tables.htm\n- Healthcare occupations: https://www.bls.gov/ooh/healthcare/\n- Employment projections: https://www.bls.gov/emp/\n- Projections by occupation: https://www.bls.gov/emp/tables/occupational-projections-and-characteristics.htm\n- **What it provides**: Employment counts and wages for all healthcare occupations (physicians, nurses, allied health, health IT, administrators). National and state-level. Healthcare projected to add **2.0M jobs 2024-2034** (8.4% growth, fastest of any sector).\n- **Update frequency**: OEWS annual (May data release); projections every 2 years\n- **Market sizing use**: Workforce volume anchors staffing technology, workforce management, and training market sizing. Wage data feeds productivity/ROI calculations.\n- **Example**: \"4.2M registered nurses × X% turnover × $Y cost per hire = workforce management TAM\"\n\n---\n\n### TIER 7 — Census Bureau\n\n---\n\n**7.1 County Business Patterns (CBP)**\n\n- Main: https://www.census.gov/programs-surveys/cbp.html\n- 2023 data release: https://www.census.gov/newsroom/press-releases/2025/2023-county-business-patterns.html\n- **What it provides**: Establishment counts, employment, payroll by NAICS industry code down to county level. Healthcare codes: 622xx (hospitals), 6211 (physician offices), 6231 (nursing homes), etc. 2023 data released June 2025; 2024 data expected summer 2026.\n- **Update frequency**: Annual (18-month lag)\n- **Market sizing use**: Derives physician practice counts and specialty breakdowns. Ambulatory care market sizing. More granular than AHA for non-hospital provider entities.\n- **Example**: \"87,000+ physician office establishments (NAICS 6211) → medical group IT TAM\"\n\n---\n\n### TIER 8 — International Sources\n\n---\n\n**8.1 WHO Global Health Expenditure Database (GHED)**\n\n- Main: https://apps.who.int/nha/database/\n- **What it provides**: Health expenditure for **190+ countries** from 2000 forward. 275 health financing indicators. Decomposed by financing source (government, private, OOP), function (curative, preventive), and provider type. December 2025 update is most current.\n- **Update frequency**: Annual (December release)\n- **Market sizing use**: Primary anchor for international market sizing. Enables country-level TAM calculation using per-capita spend × population.\n\n---\n\n**8.2 OECD Health Statistics / Health at a Glance 2025**\n\n- Main database: https://www.oecd.org/en/data/datasets/oecd-health-statistics.html\n- Health at a Glance 2025: https://www.oecd.org/en/publications/health-at-a-glance-2025_8f9e3f98-en.html\n- Health spending indicator: https://www.oecd.org/en/data/indicators/health-spending.html\n- Health spending projections: https://www.oecd.org/en/publications/2025/11/health-at-a-glance-2025_a894f72e/full-report/health-spending-projections_d3702f1a.html\n- **What it provides**: Comparable health spending, resources, and quality data for **38 OECD member countries**. Per-capita spending, % of GDP, public vs private split, hospital beds per 1,000, physician density. Health at a Glance 2025 published November 2025.\n- **Update frequency**: Annual (November/December)\n- **Market sizing use**: Cross-country market comparisons. Identifies which OECD markets are underinvested relative to GDP (sizing opportunity) vs saturated.\n\n---\n\n**8.3 NHS England Spending Data**\n\n- What we spend: https://www.england.nhs.uk/contact-us/pub-scheme/spend/\n- Financial performance: https://www.england.nhs.uk/long-read/financial-performance-update-6/\n- National Schedule of NHS Costs: https://app.powerbi.com/view?r=eyJrIjoiNjI5YjA1OWMtOGNmOC00NGQzLWIxZDYtZDAyMDQ5YWVkZjU0IiwidCI6IjM3YzM1NGIyLTg1YjAtNDdmNS1iMjIyLTA3YjQ4ZDc3NGVlMyJ9\n- **What it provides**: NHS England total budget (~£170B+), decomposed by commissioning category (acute, mental health, primary care, community). Provider-level contract values.\n- **Update frequency**: Quarterly financial performance; annual schedule of costs\n- **Market sizing use**: UK NHS TAM sizing. Identifies acute vs primary vs community spend ratios to weight product-market fit for NHS buyers.\n\n---\n\n**8.4 UK Care Quality Commission (CQC) Provider Data**\n\n- Main: https://www.cqc.org.uk/\n- Data access: https://www.cqc.org.uk/about-us/transparency/using-cqc-data\n- **What it provides**: All registered healthcare and social care providers in England. Provider counts by type (hospitals, GP practices, care homes, mental health, dental). Ratings data. API updated daily. As of March 2026: 3,900+ services assessed under single assessment framework.\n- **Update frequency**: Daily (API); monthly (downloadable files)\n- **Market sizing use**: UK provider entity count anchor. Sizes NHS digital health, care home management, and social care technology markets.\n\n---\n\n**8.5 UAE Ministry of Health and Prevention (MOHAP)**\n\n- Main: https://mohap.gov.ae/en/\n- Health Statistics: https://mohap.gov.ae/en/w/health-statistics\n- Open Data: https://mohap.gov.ae/en/open-data/mohap-open-data\n- Emirates Health Services: https://www.ehs.gov.ae/en/open-data/numbers-and-statistics\n- Abu Dhabi DOH Open Data: https://www.doh.gov.ae/resources/opendata\n- **What it provides**: Hospital counts, bed capacity, physician counts, health spending by emirate. National Health and Nutrition Survey 2024-2025 released 2025. Provider licensing data.\n- **Update frequency**: Annual statistics; periodic surveys\n- **Market sizing use**: UAE healthcare market ~$30-35B. Provider counts by emirate for facility-level TAM.\n\n---\n\n**8.6 Malaysia Ministry of Health**\n\n- Main: https://moh.gov.my/\n- Statistics & Reports: https://moh.gov.my/en/component/content/category/penerbitan-dan-laporan/infographic-reports-statistic\n- KKMNOW Open Data: https://data.moh.gov.my/\n- MOH Expenditure: https://data.moh.gov.my/data-catalogue/mnha_moh\n- NHMS 2025: https://iku.moh.gov.my/nhms2025\n- Health Facts 2024 PDF: https://www.moh.gov.my/moh/resources/Penerbitan/Penerbitan%20Utama/HEALTH%20FACTS/Health_Facts_2024.pdf\n- **What it provides**: MOH total allocation 2024: RM41.2B (~$9B USD). Hospital counts, bed counts, physician density. NHMS 2025 focused on older persons health.\n- **Update frequency**: Annual (Health Facts); survey every 3-4 years (NHMS)\n- **Market sizing use**: Malaysia healthcare TAM sizing. Growing middle-income market with government-driven expansion.\n\n---\n\n### TIER 9 — Industry Associations\n\n---\n\n**9.1 AHIP (America's Health Insurance Plans)**\n\n- Main: https://www.ahip.org/\n- Health Coverage State-to-State 2025: https://www.ahip.org/resources/health-coverage-state-to-state-2025\n- **What it provides**: State-level commercial health plan enrollment. HSA-eligible plan enrollment: **38.8M** (as of January 2024, up from 32.1M in 2019). MA: 34M+ enrollees in 2025. LTCI: 6.9M covered nationwide.\n- **Update frequency**: Annual report\n- **Market sizing use**: Commercial insurance plan market structure. Health plan entity counts and enrollment for payer-facing solution sizing.\n\n---\n\n**9.2 CAQH Index (Administrative Simplification)**\n\n- Main: https://www.caqh.org/insights/caqh-index-report\n- 2025 Index: https://www.caqh.org/blog/2025-caqh-index-shows-u.s.-healthcare-avoided-258-billion-and-accelerated-automation-interoperability-and-ai-adoption\n- **What it provides**: Administrative transaction volume and cost benchmarks across 600+ provider organizations and health plans (63% of insured lives). 2025 Index: **$258B in administrative costs avoided** through electronic transactions in 2024. Transaction automation rates by type.\n- **Update frequency**: Annual (released February)\n- **Market sizing use**: RCM automation TAM sizing. Establishes remaining manual transaction volume — the market for automation. Identifies which transaction types have highest cost-per-manual-transaction.\n\n---\n\n**9.3 CHIME / AEHIS**\n\n- Main: https://chimecentral.org/\n- **What it provides**: CHIME: **3,000+ CIO/CMIO/CDIO members** across 58 countries. AEHIS: **600+ healthcare CISO members**. Digital Health Most Wired survey (hospital digital maturity benchmark).\n- **Update frequency**: Annual (Most Wired); continuous membership\n- **Market sizing use**: CIO/CISO buyer universe count. Most Wired survey benchmarks hospital digital maturity — segments \"leading\" vs \"lagging\" technology adopters.\n\n---\n\n**9.4 HIMSS**\n\n- Main: https://www.himss.org/\n- Market Insights: https://www.himss.org/market-insights/\n- Maturity Models (EMRAM): https://www.himss.org/maturity-models/\n- **What it provides**: EMRAM scores for global hospitals. Healthcare IT adoption surveys. Cybersecurity and AI adoption benchmarks.\n- **Update frequency**: Annual surveys\n- **Market sizing use**: EHR maturity-based market segmentation for analytics and AI overlay markets.\n\n---\n\n**9.5 HFMA**\n\n- Main: https://www.hfma.org/\n- **What it provides**: **140,000+ healthcare finance professional members** nationwide. Revenue cycle benchmarks, payer contracting surveys, cost accounting guidance.\n- **Update frequency**: Annual reports\n- **Market sizing use**: Finance department buyer universe. Proxy for addressable healthcare finance buyer base.\n\n---\n\n**9.6 MGMA**\n\n- Main: https://www.mgma.com/\n- Data Reports: https://www.mgma.com/mgma-data-reports\n- 2025 Compensation Report: https://www.mgma.com/2025-provider-compensation\n- **What it provides**: Represents **15,000+ group medical practices**, **350,000+ physicians**. Compensation benchmarks, productivity data, practice management surveys.\n- **Update frequency**: Annual\n- **Market sizing use**: Physician practice entity count and economic data. Physician compensation benchmarks used to model practice revenue and derive IT spend as % of revenue.\n\n---\n\n**9.7 PhRMA**\n\n- Main: https://www.phrma.org/\n- R&D policy page: https://www.phrma.org/policy-issues/research-development\n- **What it provides**: Pharmaceutical R&D spending for member companies. 2023: **$96B global R&D spend** (21% of revenues). Members must maintain $200M+ average R&D spend and 10%+ R&D/sales ratio.\n- **Update frequency**: Annual\n- **Market sizing use**: Drug pipeline and launch services TAM. R&D spend denominator for clinical trial technology, regulatory affairs, and medical affairs solutions.\n\n---\n\n## Benchmark Targets\n\nHard anchor figures that must be verified before any bottom-up model is considered credible. All figures current as of Q1 2026.\n\n| Entity / Metric | Hard Anchor | Source | Vintage |\n|---|---|---|---|\n| Total US health spending | ~$5.0T (2024e) | CMS NHE | Dec 2024 |\n| US hospitals (all types) | 6,093 | AHA Annual Survey | Feb 2026 |\n| US hospital beds | 913,136 | AHA Annual Survey | Feb 2026 |\n| System-affiliated hospitals | 68% | AHA Fast Facts 2026 | Feb 2026 |\n| Medicare Advantage enrollees | ~34M (54%+ of Medicare) | CMS MA enrollment | Feb 2026 |\n| Medicaid + CHIP enrollees | ~76M | CMS/Medicaid.gov | Nov 2025 |\n| Medicaid enrollees in MCOs | ~80% | CMS managed care data | Annual |\n| Physician office establishments | 87,000+ (NAICS 6211) | Census CBP 2023 | Jun 2025 |\n| Medical group practices (MGMA) | 15,000+ | MGMA | Annual |\n| Physicians in MGMA groups | 350,000+ | MGMA | Annual |\n| Local health departments | 3,300+ | NACCHO | Continuous |\n| State/territorial health agencies | 59 | ASTHO | Continuous |\n| Hospital EHR adoption (certified) | 97%+ | ONC Dashboard | Annual |\n| Admin costs avoided (electronic) | $258B (2024) | CAQH Index 2025 | Feb 2026 |\n| Healthcare finance professionals | 140,000+ | HFMA | Continuous |\n| Health IT CIOs (CHIME) | 3,000+ | CHIME | Continuous |\n| Healthcare CISOs (AEHIS) | 600+ | AEHIS | Continuous |\n| HSA-eligible plan enrollees | 38.8M | AHIP | Jan 2024 |\n| Novel drugs approved (2025) | 46 | FDA | Dec 2025 |\n| PhRMA member R&D spend | $96B (2023) | PhRMA | Annual |\n| WHO GHED country coverage | 190+ countries | WHO GHED | Dec 2025 |\n\n---\n\n## Synthesis\n\n**What is well-anchored (hard data, current, cross-verified)**\n\nThe AHA Fast Facts (6,093 hospitals) is the gold standard for hospital entity counts — cross-verifiable against HCRIS cost reports, which have ~6,000+ filings. These two must agree within 5%. CMS Medicare enrollment is monthly and granular to county level — the most frequently updated enrollment data in US healthcare. NHE total spending is the only authoritative national denominator; no other source should serve as the primary spending anchor. ONC Dashboard is authoritative for hospital EHR adoption (97%+), meaning the market has definitively shifted from greenfield EHR to analytics and interoperability overlay.\n\n**What requires triangulation (survey data, methodological variation)**\n\nPhysician practice counts: CBP counts establishments, not practices or individual physicians. Cross-reference AMA Physician Masterfile (paid) for individual physician counts and MGMA for group practice economics. Health plan entity counts: AHIP and CMS cover their respective segments, but counting total unique health plan legal entities requires state insurance department filings. International market sizes: WHO GHED and OECD provide spending data reliably; provider entity counts (hospitals, clinics) for international markets vary widely in quality. Public health IT budgets: NACCHO and ASTHO provide entity counts but LHD IT budgets are not publicly compiled.\n\n**What is genuinely unknown from public sources**\n\nHealth system-level IT spend by vendor is not publicly disclosed — HCRIS shows total operating expenses but not IT line items. Specialty-level physician practice EHR penetration requires MGMA surveys (paid) or ONC physician survey segmentation. Actual payer administrative cost by function (claims, utilization management, prior auth) is not available from public sources. Revenue per provider entity by geography is available for Medicare-participating hospitals via HCRIS; non-participating facilities and non-hospital providers have no equivalent public financial disclosure.\n\n---\n\n## Open Unknowns\n\n- **CMS Hospital Compare**: Under recent HHS administration changes, some quality datasets have been removed. Verify current data availability before citing any Hospital Compare metric.\n- **ONC TEFCA interoperability data**: Emerging metrics under TEFCA are not yet standardized in the ONC Dashboard. Interoperability market sizing should be treated as early-stage without hard anchors.\n- **State Medicaid MCO contract data**: CMS provides aggregate enrollment but not per-contract MCO financial data. State Medicaid agencies publish contracts but format varies widely by state.\n- **UAE and Malaysia provider counts**: Open data portals exist but update consistency is lower than US federal sources. Treat as directional, not hard anchors.\n- **LHD IT budgets**: NACCHO entity count is solid (3,300+). Actual IT budget per LHD requires primary research or NACCHO survey reports (not all editions are free).\n\n---\n\n## Recommended Next Research Steps\n\n1. **Pull and store AHA Fast Facts 2026 figures**: PDF at the verified URL above. Extract all numeric figures (hospital count by type, beds, system affiliation %) into a reference table.\n\n2. **Download CMS NHE Tables 1-21**: The historical NHE data ZIP contains spending by payer and service type in Excel format. This is the foundation for every sector-level TAM decomposition.\n\n3. **Pull HCRIS hospital-level data for unit economics**: Use NBER processed HCRIS files to compute average revenue by hospital type (critical access, community, teaching). This drives the per-entity unit economics model.\n\n4. **Validate physician practice count**: Pull CBP NAICS 6211 (Offices of Physicians) establishment count. Cross-check against MGMA 15,000+ medical groups figure to understand the size-of-entity distribution.\n\n5. **Build OECD country comparison table**: Pull health spending % of GDP and per-capita for target international markets.
